<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects_and_closely_related_languages">Dialects and closely related languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Dialects and closely related languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This list is based on <i>Swahili and Sabaki: a linguistic history</i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">Dialects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Dialects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Modern standard Swahili is based on <i>Kiunguja,</i> the dialect spoken in <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_City" title="Zanzibar City">Zanzibar City</a>, but there are numerous dialects of Swahili, some of which are mutually unintelligible, such as the following:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_dialects">Old dialects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Old dialects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Maho (2009) considers these to be distinct languages:
</p>
<ul><li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kimwani" title="Kimwani">Kimwani</a></i> is spoken in the Kerimba Islands and northern coastal Mozambique.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Bravanese_dialect" title="Bravanese dialect">Chimwiini</a></i> is spoken by the ethnic minorities in and around the town of <a href="/wiki/Barawa" title="Barawa">Barawa</a> on the southern coast of Somalia.</li>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kibajuni_dialect" title="Kibajuni dialect">Kibajuni</a></i> is spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Bajuni_people" title="Bajuni people">Bajuni</a> minority ethnic group on the coast and islands on both sides of the Somali–Kenyan border and in the <a href="/wiki/Bajuni_Islands" title="Bajuni Islands">Bajuni Islands</a> (the northern part of the Lamu archipelago) and is also called <i>Kitikuu</i> and <i>Kigunya</i>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socotra_Swahili" title="Socotra Swahili">Socotra Swahili</a> (extinct)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sidi_language" title="Sidi language">Sidi</a>, in Gujarat (extinct)</li></ul>
<p>The rest of the dialects are divided by him into two groups:
</p>
<ul><li>Mombasa–Lamu Swahili
<ul><li>Lamu
<ul><li><i>Kiamu</i> is spoken in and around the island of <a href="/wiki/Lamu" title="Lamu">Lamu</a> (Amu).</li>
<li><i>Kipate</i> is a local dialect of <a href="/wiki/Pate_Island" title="Pate Island">Pate Island</a>, considered to be closest to the original dialect of Kingozi.</li>
<li><i>Kingozi</i> is an ancient dialect spoken on the Indian Ocean coast between Lamu and Somalia and is sometimes still used in poetry. It is often considered the source of Swahili.</li></ul></li>
<li>Mombasa
<ul><li><i>Chijomvu</i> is a subdialect of the Mombasa area.</li>
<li><i>Kimvita</i> is the major dialect of Mombasa (also known as "Mvita", which means "war", in reference to the many wars which were fought over it), the other major dialect alongside Kiunguja.</li>
<li><i>Kingare</i> is the subdialect of the Mombasa area.</li></ul></li>
<li><i>Kimrima</i> is spoken around <a href="/wiki/Pangani" title="Pangani">Pangani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanga" title="Vanga">Vanga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam" title="Dar es Salaam">Dar es Salaam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rufiji_District" title="Rufiji District">Rufiji</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mafia_Island" title="Mafia Island">Mafia Island</a>.</li>
<li><i>Kiunguja</i> is spoken in <a href="/wiki/Stone_Town" title="Stone Town">Zanzibar City</a> and environs on <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Unguja (Zanzibar) Island</a>. Kitumbatu (Pemba) dialects occupy the bulk of the island.</li>
<li>Mambrui, Malindi</li>
<li><i>Chichifundi</i>, a dialect of the southern Kenya coast.</li>
<li>Chwaka</li>
<li><i>Kivumba</i>, a dialect of the southern Kenya coast.</li>
<li>Nosse Be (Madagascar)</li></ul></li>
<li>Pemba Swahili
<ul><li><i>Kipemba</i> is a local dialect of the <a href="/wiki/Pemba_Island" title="Pemba Island">Pemba Island</a>.</li>
<li><i>Kitumbatu</i> and <i>Kimakunduchi</i> are the countryside dialects of the island of Zanzibar. Kimakunduchi is a recent renaming of "Kihadimu"; the old name means "serf" and so is considered pejorative.</li>
<li>Makunduchi</li>
<li>Mafia, Mbwera</li>
<li>Kilwa (extinct)</li>
<li><i>Kimgao</i> used to be spoken around <a href="/wiki/Kilwa_District" title="Kilwa District">Kilwa District</a> and to the south.</li></ul></li></ul>
<p>Maho includes the various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comorian_language" title="Comorian language">Comorian</a> dialects as a third group. Most other authorities consider Comorian to be a <a href="/wiki/Sabaki_languages" title="Sabaki languages">Sabaki</a> language, distinct from Swahili.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_regions">Other regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Other regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">Afroasiatic</a> <a href="/wiki/Somali_language" title="Somali language">Somali language</a> predominates, a variant of Swahili referred to as <a href="/wiki/Bravanese_dialect" title="Bravanese dialect">Chimwiini</a> (also known as Chimbalazi) is spoken along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benadir" title="Benadir">Benadir</a> coast by the <a href="/wiki/Bravanese_people" title="Bravanese people">Bravanese people</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ethnolsom_56-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnolsom-56">[56]</a></sup> Another Swahili dialect known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kibajuni_dialect" title="Kibajuni dialect">Kibajuni</a> also serves as the mother tongue of the <a href="/wiki/Bajuni_people" title="Bajuni people">Bajuni</a> minority ethnic group, which lives in the tiny <a href="/wiki/Bajuni_Islands" title="Bajuni Islands">Bajuni Islands</a> as well as the southern <a href="/wiki/Kismayo" title="Kismayo">Kismayo</a> region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ethnolsom_56-4"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnolsom-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Godfrey_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Godfrey-77">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>, there are an estimated 22,000 people who speak Swahili.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ethnoloma_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnoloma-78">[76]</a></sup> Most are descendants of those repatriated after the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Zanzibar" title="Sultanate of Zanzibar">Sultanate of Zanzibar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-African_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-African-79">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Josephi_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Josephi-80">[78]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pidgins_and_creoles">Pidgins and creoles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Pidgins and creoles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are Swahili-based slangs, pidgins and creoles:
</p>
<ul><li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kitaa_-_Dar_es_Salaam&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kitaa - Dar es Salaam (page does not exist)">Kitaa - Dar es Salaam</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Engsh" title="Engsh">Engsh</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/KiKAR" title="KiKAR">KiKAR</a> – Swahili pidgin spoken in British colonial East Africa</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kutchi-Swahili" title="Kutchi-Swahili">Kutchi-Swahili</a> – Creole derived from Kutchi and Swahili languages</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Settler_Swahili" title="Settler Swahili">Settler Swahili</a> – Swahili pidgin from Kenya and Zambia</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sheng_slang" title="Sheng slang">Sheng slang</a> – Nairobi urban-based youth slang</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Swahili_poets">Swahili poets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Swahili poets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Shaaban_bin_Robert" title="Shaaban bin Robert">Shaaban bin Robert</a> (1909-1962), Tanzanian poet, author, and essayist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Euphrase_Kezilahabi" title="Euphrase Kezilahabi">Euphrase Kezilahabi</a> (1944-2020), Tanzanian novelist, poet, and scholar</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mathias_E._Mnyampala" title="Mathias E. Mnyampala">Mathias E. Mnyampala</a> (1917-1969), Tanzanian writer, lawyer, and poet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tumi_Molekane" title="Tumi Molekane">Tumi Molekane</a> (b. 1981), South African rapper and poet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fadhy_Mtanga" title="Fadhy Mtanga">Fadhy Mtanga</a> (b. 1981), Tanzanian creative writer, photographer, graphic designer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Mwashinga" title="Christopher Mwashinga">Christopher Mwashinga</a> (b. 1965), Tanzanian author and poet</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Swahili_sayings">Swahili sayings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Swahili_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Swahili sayings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elephants_fight_Amboseli_(7234358288)_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2563" data-file-width="3844" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Elephants_fight_Amboseli_%287234358288%29_%282%29.jpg/220px-Elephants_fight_Amboseli_%287234358288%29_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Elephants_fight_Amboseli_%287234358288%29_%282%29.jpg/330px-Elephants_fight_Amboseli_%287234358288%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Elephants_fight_Amboseli_%287234358288%29_%282%29.jpg/440px-Elephants_fight_Amboseli_%287234358288%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Elephants_fight_Amboseli_(7234358288)_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loxodonta_africana" title="Loxodonta africana">Loxodonta africana</a> elephants frolic in <a href="/wiki/Amboseli_National_Park" title="Amboseli National Park">Amboseli National Park</a>, Kenya, 2012.</div></div></div>
<p>Two sayings with the same meaning of <i>Where elephants fight, the grass is trampled</i>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Wapiganapo</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tembo</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nyasi</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">huumia</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup></p></div><p style="display: none;">Wapiganapo tembo nyasi huumia</p><p style="clear: left;">Fighting elephants damage the grass.</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Ndovu</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">wawili</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">wakisongana,</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ziumiazo</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ni</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nyika.</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup></p></div><p style="display: none;">Ndovu wawili wakisongana, ziumiazo ni nyika.</p><p style="clear: left;">Where two elephants argue, the grassland is damaged.</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:0em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Mwacha</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mila</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ni</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="sw" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mtumwa.</p></div><p style="display: none;">Mwacha mila ni mtumwa.</p><p style="clear: left;">The person who abandons his culture, is a servant.</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
